\subsection{Detailed Description}
\subsubsection*{template$<$typename Derived$>$class Matrix\-Base$<$ Derived $>$}

Base class for all matrices, vectors, and expressions. 

This class is the base that is inherited by all matrix, vector, and expression types. Most of the \hyperlink{namespace_eigen}{Eigen} A\-P\-I is contained in this class. Other important classes for the \hyperlink{namespace_eigen}{Eigen} A\-P\-I are \hyperlink{class_matrix}{Matrix}, \hyperlink{class_cwise}{Cwise}, and \hyperlink{class_partial_redux}{Partial\-Redux}.

Note that some methods are defined in the Array module.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em Derived} & is the derived type, e.\-g. a matrix type, or an expression, etc.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
When writing a function taking \hyperlink{namespace_eigen}{Eigen} objects as argument, if you want your function to take as argument any matrix, vector, or expression, just let it take a \hyperlink{class_matrix_base}{Matrix\-Base} argument. As an example, here is a function print\-First\-Row which, given a matrix, vector, or expression {\itshape x}, prints the first row of {\itshape x}.


\begin{DoxyCode}
\textcolor{keyword}{template}<\textcolor{keyword}{typename} Derived>
\textcolor{keywordtype}{void} printFirstRow(\textcolor{keyword}{const} Eigen::MatrixBase<Derived>& x)
\{
  cout << x.row(0) << endl;
\}
\end{DoxyCode}

\hypertarget{class_matrix_base_a634804c67de40fec74e3640bc229364c}{\index{Matrix\-Base@{Matrix\-Base}!Real\-Scalar@{Real\-Scalar}}
\index{Real\-Scalar@{Real\-Scalar}!MatrixBase@{Matrix\-Base}}
\subsubsection[{Real\-Scalar}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}template$<$typename Derived$>$ typedef {\bf Num\-Traits}$<${\bf Scalar}$>$\-::Real {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$\-::{\bf Real\-Scalar}}}\label{class_matrix_base_a634804c67de40fec74e3640bc229364c}
This is the \char`\"{}real scalar\char`\"{} type; if the {\itshape Scalar} type is already real numbers (e.\-g. int, float or double) then {\itshape Real\-Scalar} is just the same as {\itshape Scalar}. If {\itshape Scalar} is {\itshape std\-::complex$<$\-T$>$} then Real\-Scalar is {\itshape T}.

\index{Max\-Rows\-At\-Compile\-Time@{Max\-Rows\-At\-Compile\-Time}!Matrix\-Base@{Matrix\-Base}}\index{Matrix\-Base@{Matrix\-Base}!Max\-Rows\-At\-Compile\-Time@{Max\-Rows\-At\-Compile\-Time}}\item[{\em 
\hypertarget{class_matrix_base_aaa53a8ec1bc1ba52b1e50631dac15d6da73ed130d060f18903c34624ccb8c9894}{Max\-Rows\-At\-Compile\-Time}\label{class_matrix_base_aaa53a8ec1bc1ba52b1e50631dac15d6da73ed130d060f18903c34624ccb8c9894}
}]This value is equal to the maximum possible number of rows that this expression might have. If this expression might have an arbitrarily high number of rows, this value is set to {\itshape Dynamic}.

This value is useful to know when evaluating an expression, in order to determine whether it is possible to avoid doing a dynamic memory allocation.

an expression of the adjoint (i.\-e. conjugate transpose) of $\ast$this.
\end{DoxyReturn}
Example\-:
\begin{DoxyCodeInclude}
\end{DoxyCodeInclude}
 Output\-:
\begin{DoxyVerbInclude}
\end{DoxyVerbInclude}


\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
If you want to replace a matrix by its own adjoint, do {\bfseries N\-O\-T} do this\-: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
\hyperlink{glext_8h_af593500c283bf1a787a6f947f503a5c2}{m} = \hyperlink{glext_8h_af593500c283bf1a787a6f947f503a5c2}{m}.adjoint(); \textcolor{comment}{// bug!!! caused by aliasing effect}
\end{DoxyCode}
 Instead, do\-: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
\hyperlink{glext_8h_af593500c283bf1a787a6f947f503a5c2}{m} = \hyperlink{glext_8h_af593500c283bf1a787a6f947f503a5c2}{m}.adjoint().eval();
\end{DoxyCode}

\end{DoxyWarning}

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
Even though the returned expression has dynamic size, in the case when it is applied to a fixed-\/size matrix, it inherits a fixed maximal size, which means that evaluating it does not cause a dynamic memory allocation.
\end{DoxyNote}

since block is a templated member, the keyword template has to be used if the matrix type is also a template parameter\-:
\begin{DoxyCode}
\hyperlink{glext_8h_af593500c283bf1a787a6f947f503a5c2}{m}.template block<3,3>(1,1); 
\end{DoxyCode}

\end{DoxyNote}

Short version\-: don't use this function, use \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_aeecb481d4f5f13a17a4ef74ac47e8dc9}{operator()(int,int) const } instead.

Long version\-: this function is similar to \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_aeecb481d4f5f13a17a4ef74ac47e8dc9}{operator()(int,int) const }, but without the assertion. \hypertarget{class_matrix_base_a06986b94e4841f54bb8c6bd9473f0798}{\index{Matrix\-Base@{Matrix\-Base}!Constant@{Constant}}
\index{Constant@{Constant}!MatrixBase@{Matrix\-Base}}
\subsubsection[{Constant}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}template$<$typename Derived $>$ E\-I\-G\-E\-N\-\_\-\-S\-T\-R\-O\-N\-G\-\_\-\-I\-N\-L\-I\-N\-E const {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$\-::{\bf Constant\-Return\-Type} {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$\-::Constant (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{{\bf int}}]{rows, }
\item[{{\bf int}}]{cols, }
\item[{const {\bf Scalar} \&}]{value}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}}\label{class_matrix_base_a06986b94e4841f54bb8c6bd9473f0798}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of a constant matrix of value {\itshape value} 
\end{DoxyReturn}
The parameters {\itshape rows} and {\itshape cols} are the number of rows and of columns of the returned matrix. Must be compatible with this \hyperlink{class_matrix_base}{Matrix\-Base} type.

This variant is meant to be used for dynamic-\/size matrix types. For fixed-\/size types, it is redundant to pass {\itshape rows} and {\itshape cols} as arguments, so \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_a80d399408db12eb60957efa2d7e8d4a9}{Zero()} should be used instead.

The template parameter {\itshape Custom\-Nullary\-Op} is the type of the functor.

\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em type} & the type of corner. Can be {\itshape Eigen\-::\-Top\-Left}, {\itshape Eigen\-::\-Top\-Right}, {\itshape Eigen\-::\-Bottom\-Left}, {\itshape Eigen\-::\-Bottom\-Right}. \\
\hline
{\em c\-Rows} & the number of rows in the corner \\
\hline
{\em c\-Cols} & the number of columns in the corner\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
Block\-Corner\-Dynamic\-Size  How to reference a sub-\/corner of a matrix

Example\-:
\begin{DoxyCodeInclude}
\end{DoxyCodeInclude}
 Output\-:
\begin{DoxyVerbInclude}
\end{DoxyVerbInclude}


\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
Even though the returned expression has dynamic size, in the case when it is applied to a fixed-\/size matrix, it inherits a fixed maximal size, which means that evaluating it does not cause a dynamic memory allocation.
\end{DoxyNote}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the identity matrix (not necessarily square).
\end{DoxyReturn}
The parameters {\itshape rows} and {\itshape cols} are the number of rows and of columns of the returned matrix. Must be compatible with this \hyperlink{class_matrix_base}{Matrix\-Base} type.

This variant is meant to be used for dynamic-\/size matrix types. For fixed-\/size types, it is redundant to pass {\itshape rows} and {\itshape cols} as arguments, so \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_ae099ba9697a9989d827169994bd5728d}{Identity()} should be used instead.

\hypertarget{class_matrix_base_abd1c692a0b627f24d0953bde1c4b4de5}{\index{Matrix\-Base@{Matrix\-Base}!is\-Approx@{is\-Approx}}
\index{is\-Approx@{is\-Approx}!MatrixBase@{Matrix\-Base}}
\subsubsection[{is\-Approx}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}template$<$typename Derived $>$ template$<$typename Other\-Derived $>$ bool {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$\-::is\-Approx (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{const {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Other\-Derived $>$ \&}]{other, }
\item[{typename {\bf Num\-Traits}$<$ {\bf Scalar} $>$\-::Real}]{prec}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
) const}}\label{class_matrix_base_abd1c692a0b627f24d0953bde1c4b4de5}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
{\ttfamily true} if {\ttfamily $\ast$this} is approximately equal to {\itshape other}, within the precision determined by {\itshape prec}.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
The fuzzy compares are done multiplicatively. Two vectors $ v $ and $ w $ are considered to be approximately equal within precision $ p $ if \[ \Vert v - w \Vert \leqslant p\,\min(\Vert v\Vert, \Vert w\Vert). \] For matrices, the comparison is done using the Hilbert-\/\-Schmidt norm (aka Frobenius norm L2 norm).

Because of the multiplicativeness of this comparison, one can't use this function to check whether {\ttfamily $\ast$this} is approximately equal to the zero matrix or vector. Indeed, {\ttfamily is\-Approx(zero)} returns false unless {\ttfamily $\ast$this} itself is exactly the zero matrix or vector. If you want to test whether {\ttfamily $\ast$this} is zero, use ei\-\_\-is\-Much\-Smaller\-Than(const Real\-Scalar\&, Real\-Scalar) instead.
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See Also}
ei\-\_\-is\-Much\-Smaller\-Than(const Real\-Scalar\&, Real\-Scalar) const
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
{\ttfamily true} if {\ttfamily $\ast$this} is approximately equal to {\itshape other}, within the precision determined by {\itshape prec}.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
The fuzzy compares are done multiplicatively. Two vectors $ v $ and $ w $ are considered to be approximately equal within precision $ p $ if \[ \Vert v - w \Vert \leqslant p\,\min(\Vert v\Vert, \Vert w\Vert). \] For matrices, the comparison is done on all columns.

Because of the multiplicativeness of this comparison, one can't use this function to check whether {\ttfamily $\ast$this} is approximately equal to the zero matrix or vector. Indeed, {\ttfamily is\-Approx(zero)} returns false unless {\ttfamily $\ast$this} itself is exactly the zero matrix or vector. If you want to test whether {\ttfamily $\ast$this} is zero, use ei\-\_\-is\-Much\-Smaller\-Than(const Real\-Scalar\&, Real\-Scalar) instead.
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See Also}
ei\-\_\-is\-Much\-Smaller\-Than(const Real\-Scalar\&, Real\-Scalar) const 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

Definition at line 333 of file Part.\-h.

\hypertarget{class_matrix_base_a7d53f3d135942e8ac49f16b79a2441ba}{\index{Matrix\-Base@{Matrix\-Base}!is\-Much\-Smaller\-Than@{is\-Much\-Smaller\-Than}}
\index{is\-Much\-Smaller\-Than@{is\-Much\-Smaller\-Than}!MatrixBase@{Matrix\-Base}}
\subsubsection[{is\-Much\-Smaller\-Than}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}template$<$typename Derived$>$ template$<$typename Derived $>$ bool {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$\-::is\-Much\-Smaller\-Than (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{const typename {\bf Num\-Traits}$<$ {\bf Scalar} $>$\-::Real \&}]{other, }
\item[{typename {\bf Num\-Traits}$<$ {\bf Scalar} $>$\-::Real}]{prec}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
) const}}\label{class_matrix_base_a7d53f3d135942e8ac49f16b79a2441ba}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
{\ttfamily true} if the norm of {\ttfamily $\ast$this} is much smaller than {\itshape other}, within the precision determined by {\itshape prec}.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
The fuzzy compares are done multiplicatively. A vector $ v $ is considered to be much smaller than $ x $ within precision $ p $ if \[ \Vert v \Vert \leqslant p\,\vert x\vert. \]
\end{DoxyNote}
For matrices, the comparison is done using the Hilbert-\/\-Schmidt norm. For this reason, the value of the reference scalar {\itshape other} should come from the Hilbert-\/\-Schmidt norm of a reference matrix of same dimensions.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See Also}
\hyperlink{class_matrix_base_a85eb8c7adf519acfa5b74545a6870945}{is\-Approx()}, \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_a61eb3a78243a6cc0c389978efc249f93}{is\-Much\-Smaller\-Than(const Matrix\-Base$<$\-Other\-Derived$>$\&, Real\-Scalar) const}
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
{\ttfamily true} if the norm of {\ttfamily $\ast$this} is much smaller than {\itshape other}, within the precision determined by {\itshape prec}.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
The fuzzy compares are done multiplicatively. A vector $ v $ is considered to be much smaller than $ x $ within precision $ p $ if \[ \Vert v \Vert \leqslant p\,\vert x\vert. \] For matrices, the comparison is done on all columns.
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See Also}
\hyperlink{class_matrix_base_a85eb8c7adf519acfa5b74545a6870945}{is\-Approx()}, \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_a61eb3a78243a6cc0c389978efc249f93}{is\-Much\-Smaller\-Than(const Matrix\-Base$<$\-Other\-Derived$>$\&, Real\-Scalar) const} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\hypertarget{class_matrix_base_a7d284ed351138bc583d225530c1c86e4}{\index{Matrix\-Base@{Matrix\-Base}!is\-Unitary@{is\-Unitary}}

\subsubsection[{is\-Unitary}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}template$<$typename Derived $>$ bool {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$\-::is\-Unitary (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{{\bf Real\-Scalar}}]{prec = {\ttfamily {\bf precision}$<${\bf Scalar}$>$()}}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
) const}}\label{class_matrix_base_a7d284ed351138bc583d225530c1c86e4}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
true if $\ast$this is approximately an unitary matrix, within the precision given by {\itshape prec}. In the case where the {\itshape Scalar} type is real numbers, a unitary matrix is an orthogonal matrix, whence the name.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
This can be used to check whether a family of vectors forms an orthonormal basis. Indeed, {\ttfamily m.\-is\-Unitary()} returns true if and only if the columns (equivalently, the rows) of m form an orthonormal basis.
\end{DoxyNote}

Definition at line 215 of file L\-L\-T.\-h.

\hypertarget{class_matrix_base_ac103af038592a18d277b1a27abeb4091}{\index{Matrix\-Base@{Matrix\-Base}!lp\-Norm@{lp\-Norm}}
\index{lp\-Norm@{lp\-Norm}!MatrixBase@{Matrix\-Base}}
\subsubsection[{lp\-Norm}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}template$<$typename Derived$>$ template$<$int p$>$ {\bf Num\-Traits}$<$typename {\bf ei\-\_\-traits}$<$Derived$>$\-::{\bf Scalar}$>$\-::Real {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$\-::lp\-Norm (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
{}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}}\label{class_matrix_base_ac103af038592a18d277b1a27abeb4091}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
the $ \ell^p $ norm of $\ast$this, that is, returns the p-\/th root of the sum of the p-\/th powers of the absolute values of the coefficients of $\ast$this. If {\itshape p} is the special value {\itshape Eigen\-::\-Infinity}, this function returns the $ \ell^p\infty $ norm, that is the maximum of the absolute values of the coefficients of $\ast$this.
\end{DoxyReturn}

\hypertarget{class_matrix_base_add33afaa49ed8ee0c5664a5288b640ed}{\index{Matrix\-Base@{Matrix\-Base}!Nullary\-Expr@{Nullary\-Expr}}
\index{Nullary\-Expr@{Nullary\-Expr}!MatrixBase@{Matrix\-Base}}
\subsubsection[{Nullary\-Expr}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}template$<$typename Derived$>$ template$<$typename Custom\-Nullary\-Op $>$ E\-I\-G\-E\-N\-\_\-\-S\-T\-R\-O\-N\-G\-\_\-\-I\-N\-L\-I\-N\-E const {\bf Cwise\-Nullary\-Op}$<$Custom\-Nullary\-Op, Derived$>$ {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$\-::Nullary\-Expr (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{{\bf int}}]{rows, }
\item[{{\bf int}}]{cols, }
\item[{const Custom\-Nullary\-Op \&}]{func}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}\label{class_matrix_base_add33afaa49ed8ee0c5664a5288b640ed}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of a matrix defined by a custom functor {\itshape func} 
\end{DoxyReturn}
The parameters {\itshape rows} and {\itshape cols} are the number of rows and of columns of the returned matrix. Must be compatible with this \hyperlink{class_matrix_base}{Matrix\-Base} type.

This variant is meant to be used for dynamic-\/size matrix types. For fixed-\/size types, it is redundant to pass {\itshape rows} and {\itshape cols} as arguments, so \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_a80d399408db12eb60957efa2d7e8d4a9}{Zero()} should be used instead.

The template parameter {\itshape Custom\-Nullary\-Op} is the type of the functor.

\end{DoxyReturn}
The parameter {\itshape size} is the size of the returned vector. Must be compatible with this \hyperlink{class_matrix_base}{Matrix\-Base} type.

This variant is meant to be used for dynamic-\/size vector types. For fixed-\/size types, it is redundant to pass {\itshape size} as argument, so \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_a80d399408db12eb60957efa2d7e8d4a9}{Zero()} should be used instead.

The template parameter {\itshape Custom\-Nullary\-Op} is the type of the functor.

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of a matrix where all coefficients equal one.
\end{DoxyReturn}
The parameters {\itshape rows} and {\itshape cols} are the number of rows and of columns of the returned matrix. Must be compatible with this \hyperlink{class_matrix_base}{Matrix\-Base} type.

This variant is meant to be used for dynamic-\/size matrix types. For fixed-\/size types, it is redundant to pass {\itshape rows} and {\itshape cols} as arguments, so \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_a6ea7fe1ebd5eb078bcafa2c00d5c4021}{Ones()} should be used instead.

\hypertarget{class_matrix_base_a29c5c34c077be6a7651375b77c30b95d}{\index{Matrix\-Base@{Matrix\-Base}!Ones@{Ones}}
\index{Ones@{Ones}!MatrixBase@{Matrix\-Base}}
\subsubsection[{Ones}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}template$<$typename Derived $>$ E\-I\-G\-E\-N\-\_\-\-S\-T\-R\-O\-N\-G\-\_\-\-I\-N\-L\-I\-N\-E const {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$\-::{\bf Constant\-Return\-Type} {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$\-::Ones (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{{\bf int}}]{size}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}}\label{class_matrix_base_a29c5c34c077be6a7651375b77c30b95d}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of a vector where all coefficients equal one.
\end{DoxyReturn}
The parameter {\itshape size} is the size of the returned vector. Must be compatible with this \hyperlink{class_matrix_base}{Matrix\-Base} type.

This variant is meant to be used for dynamic-\/size vector types. For fixed-\/size types, it is redundant to pass {\itshape size} as argument, so \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_a6ea7fe1ebd5eb078bcafa2c00d5c4021}{Ones()} should be used instead.

\label{class_matrix_base_MatrixBaseCommaInitRef}%
\hypertarget{class_matrix_base_MatrixBaseCommaInitRef}{}%
Convenient operator to set the coefficients of a matrix.

The coefficients must be provided in a row major order and exactly match the size of the matrix. Otherwise an assertion is raised.

\subsubsection[{packet}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}template$<$typename Derived$>$ template$<$int Load\-Mode$>$ E\-I\-G\-E\-N\-\_\-\-S\-T\-R\-O\-N\-G\-\_\-\-I\-N\-L\-I\-N\-E {\bf ei\-\_\-packet\-\_\-traits}$<$typename {\bf ei\-\_\-traits}$<$Derived$>$\-::{\bf Scalar}$>$\-::{\bf type} {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$\-::packet (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{{\bf int}}]{row, }
\item[{{\bf int}}]{col}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
) const}}\label{class_matrix_base_ab99a7d3e1ab304a09c4da567615e0df6}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
the packet of coefficients starting at the given row and column. It is your responsibility to ensure that a packet really starts there. This method is only available on expressions having the Packet\-Access\-Bit.
\end{DoxyReturn}
The {\itshape Load\-Mode} parameter may have the value {\itshape Aligned} or {\itshape Unaligned}. Its effect is to select the appropriate vectorization instruction. Aligned access is faster, but is only possible for packets starting at an address which is a multiple of the packet size.

\subsubsection[{Random}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}template$<$typename Derived $>$ const {\bf Cwise\-Nullary\-Op}$<$ {\bf ei\-\_\-scalar\-\_\-random\-\_\-op}$<$ typename {\bf ei\-\_\-traits}$<$ Derived $>$\-::{\bf Scalar} $>$, Derived $>$ {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$\-::Random (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{{\bf int}}]{rows, }
\item[{{\bf int}}]{cols}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}, {\ttfamily [static]}}}\label{class_matrix_base_a84d2e57e9a2a4474edbefdeae7a1f9e6}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
a random matrix (not an expression, the matrix is immediately evaluated).
\end{DoxyReturn}
The parameters {\itshape rows} and {\itshape cols} are the number of rows and of columns of the returned matrix. Must be compatible with this \hyperlink{class_matrix_base}{Matrix\-Base} type.

This variant is meant to be used for dynamic-\/size matrix types. For fixed-\/size types, it is redundant to pass {\itshape rows} and {\itshape cols} as arguments, so \hyperlink{_math_functions_8h_af7765854e43088ad52641a2895321fa2}{ei\-\_\-random()} should be used instead.

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}

\hypertarget{class_matrix_base_aa338f29b37898b2104b39c32b6854a65}{\index{Matrix\-Base@{Matrix\-Base}!solve\-Triangular@{solve\-Triangular}}
\index{solve\-Triangular@{solve\-Triangular}!MatrixBase@{Matrix\-Base}}
\subsubsection[{solve\-Triangular}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}template$<$typename Derived $>$ template$<$typename Other\-Derived $>$ {\bf ei\-\_\-plain\-\_\-matrix\-\_\-type\-\_\-column\-\_\-major}$<$ Other\-Derived $>$\-::{\bf type} {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$\-::solve\-Triangular (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{const {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Other\-Derived $>$ \&}]{other}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
) const}}\label{class_matrix_base_aa338f29b37898b2104b39c32b6854a65}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
the product of the inverse of {\ttfamily $\ast$this} with {\itshape other}, {\itshape $\ast$this} being triangular.
\end{DoxyReturn}


This function computes the inverse-\/matrix matrix product inverse({\ttfamily $\ast$this}) $\ast$ {\itshape other}. The matrix {\ttfamily $\ast$this} must be triangular and invertible (i.\-e., all the coefficients of the diagonal must be non zero). It works as a forward (resp. backward) substitution if {\ttfamily $\ast$this} is an upper (resp. lower) triangular matrix.

It is required that {\ttfamily $\ast$this} be marked as either an upper or a lower triangular matrix, which can be done by \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_ae9b798d2c9da0080c4ce3b24ebc4d169}{marked()}, and that is automatically the case with expressions such as those returned by extract().

Solve\-Triangular  How to solve a triangular system (aka. how to multiply the inverse of a triangular matrix by another one)

Example\-:
\begin{DoxyCodeInclude}
\end{DoxyCodeInclude}
 Output\-:
\begin{DoxyVerbInclude}
\end{DoxyVerbInclude}


This function is essentially a wrapper to the faster \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_ab7a4ee6e139cf49ea84cf1c39d87d8ce}{solve\-Triangular\-In\-Place()} function creating a temporary copy of {\itshape other}, calling \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_ab7a4ee6e139cf49ea84cf1c39d87d8ce}{solve\-Triangular\-In\-Place()} on the copy and returning it. Therefore, if {\itshape other} is not needed anymore, it is quite faster to call \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_ab7a4ee6e139cf49ea84cf1c39d87d8ce}{solve\-Triangular\-In\-Place()} instead of \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_aa338f29b37898b2104b39c32b6854a65}{solve\-Triangular()}.

For users coming from B\-L\-A\-S, this function (and more specifically \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_ab7a4ee6e139cf49ea84cf1c39d87d8ce}{solve\-Triangular\-In\-Place()}) offer all the operations supported by the {\ttfamily $\ast$\-T\-R\-S\-V} and {\ttfamily $\ast$\-T\-R\-S\-M} B\-L\-A\-S routines.

{\bfseries Tips\-:} to perform a {\itshape \char`\"{}right-\/inverse-\/multiply\char`\"{}} you can simply transpose the operation, e.\-g.\-: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
M * T^1  <=>  T.transpose().solveTriangularInPlace(M.transpose());
\end{DoxyCode}


\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See Also}
\hyperlink{class_matrix_base_ab7a4ee6e139cf49ea84cf1c39d87d8ce}{solve\-Triangular\-In\-Place()}, \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_ae9b798d2c9da0080c4ce3b24ebc4d169}{marked()}, extract() 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\hypertarget{class_matrix_base_a794fe4b04caa197931bb688ce0dc7e43}{\index{Matrix\-Base@{Matrix\-Base}!transpose@{transpose}}

\subsubsection[{transpose}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}template$<$typename Derived $>$ {\bf Transpose}$<$ Derived $>$ {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$\-::{\bf transpose} (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
{}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}}\label{class_matrix_base_a794fe4b04caa197931bb688ce0dc7e43}

an expression of the transpose of $\ast$this.
\end{DoxyReturn}
Example\-:
\begin{DoxyCodeInclude}
\end{DoxyCodeInclude}
 Output\-:
\begin{DoxyVerbInclude}
\end{DoxyVerbInclude}


\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
If you want to replace a matrix by its own transpose, do {\bfseries N\-O\-T} do this\-: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
\hyperlink{glext_8h_af593500c283bf1a787a6f947f503a5c2}{m} = \hyperlink{glext_8h_af593500c283bf1a787a6f947f503a5c2}{m}.transpose(); \textcolor{comment}{// bug!!! caused by aliasing effect}
\end{DoxyCode}
 Instead, use the \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_afabc132dde4af8bf9b558e7caa13dc0e}{transpose\-In\-Place()} method\-: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
\hyperlink{glext_8h_af593500c283bf1a787a6f947f503a5c2}{m}.transposeInPlace();
\end{DoxyCode}
 which gives \hyperlink{namespace_eigen}{Eigen} good opportunities for optimization, or alternatively you can also do\-: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
\hyperlink{glext_8h_af593500c283bf1a787a6f947f503a5c2}{m} = \hyperlink{glext_8h_af593500c283bf1a787a6f947f503a5c2}{m}.transpose().eval();
\end{DoxyCode}

\end{DoxyWarning}

\hypertarget{class_matrix_base_afabc132dde4af8bf9b558e7caa13dc0e}{\index{Matrix\-Base@{Matrix\-Base}!transpose\-In\-Place@{transpose\-In\-Place}}
\index{transpose\-In\-Place@{transpose\-In\-Place}!MatrixBase@{Matrix\-Base}}
\subsubsection[{transpose\-In\-Place}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}template$<$typename Derived $>$ {\bf void} {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$\-::transpose\-In\-Place (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
{}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}}\label{class_matrix_base_afabc132dde4af8bf9b558e7caa13dc0e}
This is the \char`\"{}in place\char`\"{} version of transpose\-: it transposes {\ttfamily $\ast$this}.

In most cases it is probably better to simply use the transposed expression of a matrix. However, when transposing the matrix data itself is really needed, then this \char`\"{}in-\/place\char`\"{} version is probably the right choice because it provides the following additional features\-:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item less error prone\-: doing the same operation with .\hyperlink{class_matrix_base_a794fe4b04caa197931bb688ce0dc7e43}{transpose()} requires special care\-: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
\hyperlink{glext_8h_af593500c283bf1a787a6f947f503a5c2}{m} = \hyperlink{glext_8h_af593500c283bf1a787a6f947f503a5c2}{m}.transpose().eval(); 
\end{DoxyCode}

\item no temporary object is created (currently only for squared matrices)
\item it allows future optimizations (cache friendliness, etc.)
\end{DoxyItemize}

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
if the matrix is not square, then {\ttfamily $\ast$this} must be a resizable matrix.
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See Also}
\hyperlink{class_matrix_base_a794fe4b04caa197931bb688ce0dc7e43}{transpose()}, \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_a1b377fccb4180e17272feea7fc66b1b8}{adjoint()} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\hypertarget{class_matrix_base_a105d176348bd86b2e0d51b428eddcb4c}{\index{Matrix\-Base@{Matrix\-Base}!unit\-Orthogonal@{unit\-Orthogonal}}
\index{unit\-Orthogonal@{unit\-Orthogonal}!MatrixBase@{Matrix\-Base}}
\subsubsection[{unit\-Orthogonal}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}template$<$typename Derived $>$ {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$\-::{\bf Plain\-Matrix\-Type} {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$\-::unit\-Orthogonal (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{{\bf void}}]{}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
) const}}\label{class_matrix_base_a105d176348bd86b2e0d51b428eddcb4c}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
a unit vector which is orthogonal to {\ttfamily $\ast$this} 
\end{DoxyReturn}
The size of {\ttfamily $\ast$this} must be at least 2. If the size is exactly 2, then the returned vector is a counter clock wise rotation of {\ttfamily $\ast$this}, i.\-e., (-\/y,x).\hyperlink{class_matrix_base_a65f587dc428711338002878c561bff6f}{normalized()}.

\hypertarget{class_matrix_base_a67e9a55a7fb7a5f59c9f3e5f34bf639f}{\index{Matrix\-Base@{Matrix\-Base}!visit@{visit}}
\index{visit@{visit}!MatrixBase@{Matrix\-Base}}
\subsubsection[{visit}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}template$<$typename Derived $>$ template$<$typename Visitor $>$ {\bf void} {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$\-::visit (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{Visitor \&}]{visitor}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
) const}}\label{class_matrix_base_a67e9a55a7fb7a5f59c9f3e5f34bf639f}
Applies the visitor {\itshape visitor} to the whole coefficients of the matrix or vector.

The template parameter {\itshape Visitor} is the type of the visitor and provides the following interface\-: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
\textcolor{keyword}{struct }MyVisitor \{
  \textcolor{comment}{// called for the first coefficient}
  \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} init(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_a625df8339dc2d816cbc0fd66e7dadaf5}{Scalar}& \hyperlink{glext_8h_aa0e2e9cea7f208d28acda0480144beb0}{value}, \textcolor{keywordtype}{int} \hyperlink{analyze_i_n_s_g_p_s_8m_a6f6ccfcf58b31cb6412107d9d5281426}{i}, \textcolor{keywordtype}{int} j);
  \textcolor{comment}{// called for all other coefficients}
  \textcolor{keywordtype}{void} \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_aeecb481d4f5f13a17a4ef74ac47e8dc9}{operator() }(\textcolor{keyword}{const} \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_a625df8339dc2d816cbc0fd66e7dadaf5}{Scalar}& \hyperlink{glext_8h_aa0e2e9cea7f208d28acda0480144beb0}{value}, \textcolor{keywordtype}{int} \hyperlink{analyze_i_n_s_g_p_s_8m_a6f6ccfcf58b31cb6412107d9d5281426}{i}, \textcolor{keywordtype}{int} j);
\};
\end{DoxyCode}


\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
compared to one or two {\itshape for} {\itshape loops}, visitors offer automatic unrolling for small fixed size matrix.
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See Also}
min\-Coeff(int$\ast$,int$\ast$), max\-Coeff(int$\ast$,int$\ast$), \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_ad5e830e56b3f67a1796a553f44139e81}{Matrix\-Base\-::redux()} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\hypertarget{class_matrix_base_a6c8c385355a4c4254a921ab76dae9da7}{\index{Matrix\-Base@{Matrix\-Base}!write\-Packet@{write\-Packet}}
\index{write\-Packet@{write\-Packet}!MatrixBase@{Matrix\-Base}}
\subsubsection[{write\-Packet}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}template$<$typename Derived$>$ template$<$int Store\-Mode$>$ E\-I\-G\-E\-N\-\_\-\-S\-T\-R\-O\-N\-G\-\_\-\-I\-N\-L\-I\-N\-E {\bf void} {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$\-::write\-Packet (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{{\bf int}}]{row, }
\item[{{\bf int}}]{col, }
\item[{const typename {\bf ei\-\_\-packet\-\_\-traits}$<$ typename {\bf ei\-\_\-traits}$<$ Derived $>$\-::{\bf Scalar} $>$\-::{\bf type} \&}]{x}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}\label{class_matrix_base_a6c8c385355a4c4254a921ab76dae9da7}
Stores the given packet of coefficients, at the given row and column of this expression. It is your responsibility to ensure that a packet really starts there. This method is only available on expressions having the Packet\-Access\-Bit.

The {\itshape Load\-Mode} parameter may have the value {\itshape Aligned} or {\itshape Unaligned}. Its effect is to select the appropriate vectorization instruction. Aligned access is faster, but is only possible for packets starting at an address which is a multiple of the packet size. 

Definition at line 275 of file Coeffs.\-h.

\subsubsection[{write\-Packet}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}template$<$typename Derived$>$ template$<$int Store\-Mode$>$ {\bf void} {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$\-::write\-Packet (

\index{write\-Packet@{write\-Packet}!MatrixBase@{Matrix\-Base}}
\subsubsection[{write\-Packet}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}template$<$typename Derived$>$ template$<$int Store\-Mode$>$ E\-I\-G\-E\-N\-\_\-\-S\-T\-R\-O\-N\-G\-\_\-\-I\-N\-L\-I\-N\-E {\bf void} {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$\-::write\-Packet (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{{\bf int}}]{index, }
\item[{const typename {\bf ei\-\_\-packet\-\_\-traits}$<$ typename {\bf ei\-\_\-traits}$<$ Derived $>$\-::{\bf Scalar} $>$\-::{\bf type} \&}]{x}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}\label{class_matrix_base_acb271944fdd941de41ac40adff333f56}
Stores the given packet of coefficients, at the given index in this expression. It is your responsibility to ensure that a packet really starts there. This method is only available on expressions having the Packet\-Access\-Bit and the Linear\-Access\-Bit.

The {\itshape Load\-Mode} parameter may have the value {\itshape Aligned} or {\itshape Unaligned}. Its effect is to select the appropriate vectorization instruction. Aligned access is faster, but is only possible for packets starting at an address which is a multiple of the packet size.

\index{Zero@{Zero}!MatrixBase@{Matrix\-Base}}
\subsubsection[{Zero}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}template$<$typename Derived $>$ E\-I\-G\-E\-N\-\_\-\-S\-T\-R\-O\-N\-G\-\_\-\-I\-N\-L\-I\-N\-E const {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$\-::{\bf Constant\-Return\-Type} {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$\-::Zero (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{{\bf int}}]{rows, }
\item[{{\bf int}}]{cols}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}}\label{class_matrix_base_a29517bfa81dd52a8c7302d1902a99c2a}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of a zero matrix.
\end{DoxyReturn}
The parameters {\itshape rows} and {\itshape cols} are the number of rows and of columns of the returned matrix. Must be compatible with this \hyperlink{class_matrix_base}{Matrix\-Base} type.

This variant is meant to be used for dynamic-\/size matrix types. For fixed-\/size types, it is redundant to pass {\itshape rows} and {\itshape cols} as arguments, so \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_a80d399408db12eb60957efa2d7e8d4a9}{Zero()} should be used instead.

\hypertarget{class_matrix_base_a2b608114f7a813907b66ea1bb0dd33a3}{\index{Matrix\-Base@{Matrix\-Base}!Zero@{Zero}}
\index{Zero@{Zero}!MatrixBase@{Matrix\-Base}}
\subsubsection[{Zero}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}template$<$typename Derived $>$ E\-I\-G\-E\-N\-\_\-\-S\-T\-R\-O\-N\-G\-\_\-\-I\-N\-L\-I\-N\-E const {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$\-::{\bf Constant\-Return\-Type} {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$\-::Zero (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{{\bf int}}]{size}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}}\label{class_matrix_base_a2b608114f7a813907b66ea1bb0dd33a3}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of a zero vector.
\end{DoxyReturn}
The parameter {\itshape size} is the size of the returned vector. Must be compatible with this \hyperlink{class_matrix_base}{Matrix\-Base} type.

This variant is meant to be used for dynamic-\/size vector types. For fixed-\/size types, it is redundant to pass {\itshape size} as argument, so \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_a80d399408db12eb60957efa2d7e8d4a9}{Zero()} should be used instead.

This variant is only for fixed-\/size \hyperlink{class_matrix_base}{Matrix\-Base} types. For dynamic-\/size types, you need to use the variants taking size arguments.

\hypertarget{class_matrix_base_a7cafa3b9b77704316e5c99df5f420cdf}{\index{Matrix\-Base@{Matrix\-Base}!operator$<$$<$@{operator$<$$<$}}
\index{operator$<$$<$@{operator$<$$<$}!MatrixBase@{Matrix\-Base}}
\subsubsection[{operator$<$$<$}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}template$<$typename Derived $>$ std\-::ostream \& operator$<$$<$ (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{std\-::ostream \&}]{s, }
\item[{const {\bf Matrix\-Base}$<$ Derived $>$ \&}]{m}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [related]}}}\label{class_matrix_base_a7cafa3b9b77704316e5c99df5f420cdf}
Outputs the matrix, to the given stream.

If you wish to print the matrix with a format different than the default, use \hyperlink{class_matrix_base_a450797ce64a44162dfd4a0cbb4ea6f16}{Matrix\-Base\-::format()}.

It is also possible to change the default format by defining E\-I\-G\-E\-N\-\_\-\-D\-E\-F\-A\-U\-L\-T\-\_\-\-I\-O\-\_\-\-F\-O\-R\-M\-A\-T before including \hyperlink{namespace_eigen}{Eigen} headers. If not defined, this will automatically be defined to Eigen\-::\-I\-O\-Format(), that is the Eigen\-::\-I\-O\-Format with default parameters.

\end{DoxySeeAlso}
